     <div class="info-tile-data blog-post"> 
      <h1>How to convert text to date and number to date in Excel</h1> 
      <p class="post-meta">by <a href="https://plus.google.com/114460563248390451831?rel=author">Svetlana Cheusheva</a> <span class="tags"><a href="https://www.ablebits.com/office-addins-blog/tag/excel/" rel="tag">Excel</a>, <a href="https://www.ablebits.com/office-addins-blog/tag/excel-date/" rel="tag">Excel date</a>, <a href="https://www.ablebits.com/office-addins-blog/tag/excel-functions/" rel="tag">Excel functions</a>, <a href="https://www.ablebits.com/office-addins-blog/tag/excel-howto/" rel="tag">Excel tips</a> </span> <span class="comments"><a href="https://www.ablebits.com/office-addins-blog/2015/03/26/excel-convert-text-date/#comments">160 Comments</a></span> </p> 
     </div> 
    </div> 
    <div id="blog-post-container"> 
     <div class="info-tile blog-post" style="position: relative;"> 
      <div class="blog-post-body"> 
       <a id="dd_start"></a>
       <p><em>The tutorial explains how to use Excel functions to convert text to date and number to date, and how to turn text strings into dates in a non-formula way. You will also learn how to quickly change a number to date format.</em></p> 
       <p>Since Excel is not the only application you work with, sometimes you'll find yourself working with dates imported in an Excel worksheet from a .csv file or another external source. When that happens, chances are the dates will export as text entries. Even though they look like dates, Excel won't not recognize them as such.</p> 
       <p>There are many ways to convert text to date in Excel and this tutorial aims to cover them all, so that you can choose a text-to-date conversion technique most suitable for your data format and your preference for a formula or non-formula way.</p> 
       <ul class="nav-cat"> 
        <li><a href="#spot-text-dates">How to spot "text dates" in Excel</a></li> 
        <li><a href="#excel-convert-number-date">How to convert number to date in Excel</a></li> 
        <li><a href="#convert-text-date">How to convert text to date in Excel</a> 
         <ul class="nav"> 
          <li><a href="#excel-datevalue-function">DATEVALUE function</a></li> 
          <li><a href="#excel-value-function">VALUE function</a></li> 
          <li><a href="#alternativa-formulas">Mathematical operations</a></li> 
          <li><a href="#text2date-custom-delimiters">Converting text strings with custom delimiters</a></li> 
          <li><a href="#text-to-columns-wizard">Text to Column wizard</a></li> 
          <li><a href="#text2date-paste-special">Paste Special</a></li> 
          <li><a href="#text2date-two-digit-years">Fixing dates with two-digit years</a></li> 
         </ul> </li> 
       </ul> 
       <h2><a name="spot-text-dates"></a>How to distinguish normal Excel dates from "text dates"</h2> 
       <p>When importing data into Excel, there is often a problem with date formatting. The imported entries may look like normal Excel dates to you, but they don't behave like dates. Microsoft Excel treats such entries as text, meaning you cannot sort your table by date properly, nor can you use those "text dates" in formulas, PivotTables, charts or any other Excel tool that recognizes dates.</p> 
       <p>There are a few signs that can help you determine whether a given entry is a date or a text value.</p> 
       <table class="blog-table" border="0" cellspacing="0" cellpadding="0"> 
        <tbody> 
         <tr class="head"> 
          <td width="323"><strong>Dates</strong></td> 
          <td width="323"><strong>Text values</strong></td> 
         </tr> 
         <tr valign="top"> 
          <td> 
           <ul> 
            <li>Right-aligned by default.</li> 
            <li>Have <strong>Date</strong> format in the <em>Number Format</em> box on the <em>Home</em> tab &gt; <em>Number</em>.</li> 
            <li>If several dates are selected, the Status Bar shows <em>Average</em>, <em>Count</em> and <em>SUM</em>.</li> 
           </ul> </td> 
          <td> 
           <ul> 
            <li>Left-aligned by default.</li> 
            <li><strong>General</strong> format displays in the <em>Number Format</em> box on the <em>Home</em> tab &gt; <em>Number</em>.</li> 
            <li>If several text dates are selected, the Status Bar only shows <em>Count</em>.</li> 
            <li>There may be a leading apostrophe visible in the formula bar.</li> 
           </ul> </td> 
         </tr> 
        </tbody> 
       </table> 
       <p><img class="imgl2" src="https://cdn.ablebits.com/_img-blog/text-date/text-dates-excel.png" alt="How to distinguish dates from text strings in Excel" title="How to distinguish dates from text strings in Excel"></p> 
       <h2><a name="excel-convert-number-date"></a>How to convert number to date in Excel</h2> 
       <p>Since all Excel functions that change text to date return a number as a result, let's have a closer look at converting numbers to dates first.</p> 
       <p>As you probably know, Excel stores dates and times as serial numbers and it is only a cell's formatting that forces a number to be displayed as a date. For example, 1-Jan-1900 is stored as number 1, 2-Jan-1900 is stored as 2, and 1-Jan-2015 is stored as 42005. For more information on how Excel stores dates and times, please see <a href="https://www.ablebits.com/office-addins-blog/2015/03/11/change-date-format-excel/#excel-date-format">Excel date format</a>.</p> 
       <p>When calculating dates in Excel, the result returned by different <a href="https://www.ablebits.com/office-addins-blog/2015/06/10/excel-date-functions/">date functions</a> is often a serial number representing a date. To convert such serial number to date in Excel, all you have to do is change the cell formatting. For this, select a cell or a range of cells with the numbers you want to convert to dates and press <span class="hkey-hlight">Ctrl+1</span> to open the <em>Format Cells</em> dialog. On the <em>Number</em> tab, choose <strong>Date</strong>, select the desired date format under <em>Type</em> and click OK.<br> <img class="imgl2" src="https://cdn.ablebits.com/_img-blog/text-date/convert-number-date.png" alt="Converting numbers to dates in Excel" title="Converting numbers to dates in Excel"></p> 
       <p>Yep, it's that easy! If you want something more sophisticated than predefined Excel date formats, please see <a href="https://www.ablebits.com/office-addins-blog/2015/03/11/change-date-format-excel/#custom-date-format">how to create a custom date format in Excel</a>.</p> 
       <p>If some stubborn number refuses to change to a date, check out <a href="https://www.ablebits.com/office-addins-blog/2015/03/11/change-date-format-excel/#solutions-date-format-not-working">Excel date format not working - troubleshooting tips</a>.</p> 
       <h3><a name="convert-8number-digits-date"></a>How to convert 8-digit number to date in Excel</h3> 
       <p>It's a very common situation when a date is input as an 8-digit number like 10032016, and you need to convert it into a date value that Excel can recognize (10/03/2016). In this case, simply changing the cell format to Date won't work - you will get ########## as the result.</p> 
       <p>To convert such a number to date, you will have to use the <a href="https://www.ablebits.com/office-addins-blog/2015/06/10/excel-date-functions/#DATE-function">DATE function</a> in combination with RIGHT, LEFT and MID functions. Unfortunately, it is not possible to make a universal formula that will work in all scenarios because the original number can be input in a variety of different formats. For example:</p> 
       <table class="blog-table" border="0" cellspacing="0" cellpadding="0"> 
        <tbody> 
         <tr class="head"> 
          <td>Number</td> 
          <td>Format</td> 
          <td>Date</td> 
         </tr> 
         <tr> 
          <td>10032016</td> 
          <td>ddmmyyyy</td> 
          <td rowspan="3">10-Mar-2016</td> 
         </tr> 
         <tr> 
          <td>20160310</td> 
          <td>yyyymmdd</td> 
         </tr> 
         <tr> 
          <td>20161003</td> 
          <td>yyyyddmm</td> 
         </tr> 
        </tbody> 
       </table> 
       <p>Anyway, I will try to explain the general approach to converting such numbers to dates and provide a few formula examples.</p> 
       <p>For starters, remember the order of the Excel Date function arguments:</p> 
       <div class="xl-formula">
        =DATE(year, month, day)
       </div> 
       <p>So, what you need to do is extract a year, month and date from the original number and supply them as the corresponding arguments to the Date function.</p> 
       <p>For example, let's see how you can convert number 10032016 (stored in cell A1) to date 3/10/2016.</p> 
       <ul> 
        <li>Extract the <strong>year</strong>. It's the last 4 digits, so we use the RIGHT function to pick the last 4 characters: RIGHT(A1, 4).</li> 
        <li>Extract the <strong>month</strong>. It's the 3<sup>rd</sup> and 4<sup>th</sup> digits, so we employ the MID function to get them MID(A1, 3, 2). Where 3 (second argument) is the start number, and 2 (third argument) is the number of characters to extract.</li> 
        <li>Extract the <strong>day</strong>. It's the first 2 digits, so we have the LEFT function to return the first 2 characters: LEFT(A2,2).</li> 
       </ul> 
       <p>Finally, embed the above ingredients into the Date function, and you get a formula to convert number to date in Excel:</p> 
       <p><code>=DATE(RIGHT(A1,4), MID(A1,3,2), LEFT(A1,2))</code></p> 
       <p>The following screenshot demonstrates this and a couple more formulas in action:<br> <img class="imgl2" src="https://cdn.ablebits.com/_img-blog/text-date/convert-number-date-excel.png" alt="Converting number to date in Excel" title="Converting number to date in Excel"></p> 
       <p>Please pay attention to the last formula in the above screenshot (row 6). The original number-date (161003) contains only 2 chars representing a year (16). So, to get the year of 2016, we concatenate 20 and 16 using the following formula: 20&amp;LEFT(A6,2). If you don't do this, the Date function will return 1916 by default, which is a bit weird as if Microsoft still lived in the 20<sup>th</sup> century :)</p> 
       <div class="sm-note">
        <b>Note.</b> The formulas demonstrated in this example work correctly as long as 
        <strong>all numbers</strong> you want to convert to dates follow the 
        <strong>same pattern</strong>.
       </div> 
       <h2><a name="convert-text-date"></a>How to convert text to date in Excel</h2> 
       <p>When you spot text dates in your Excel file, most likely you would want to convert those text strings to normal Excel dates so that you can refer to them in your formulas to perform various calculations. And as is often the case in Excel, there are a few ways to tackle the task.</p> 
       <h3><a name="excel-datevalue-function"></a>Excel DATEVALUE function - change text to date</h3> 
       <p>The <strong>DATEVALUE</strong> function in Excel converts a date in the text format to a serial number that Excel recognizes as a date.</p> 
       <p>The syntax of Excel's DATEVALUE is very straightforward:</p> 
       <p><code>=DATEVALUE(date_text)</code></p> 
       <p>So, the formula to convert a text value to date is as simple as <code>=DATEVALUE(A1)</code>, where A1 is a cell with a date stored as a text string.</p> 
       <p>Because the Excel DATEVALUE function converts a text date to a serial number, you will have to make that number look like a date by <a href="#excel-convert-number-date">applying the Date format</a> to it, as we discussed a moment ago.</p> 
       <p>The following screenshots demonstrates a few Excel DATEVALUE formulas in action:<br> <img class="imgl2" src="https://cdn.ablebits.com/_img-blog/text-date/excel-datevalue-function.png" alt="Convert text to date using the Excel DATEVALUE function." title="Convert text to date using the Excel DATEVALUE function."></p> 
       <h4>Excel DATEVALUE function - things to remember</h4> 
       <p>When converting a text string to a date using the DATEVALUE function, please keep in mind that:</p> 
       <ul> 
        <li>Time information in text strings is ignored, as you can see in rows 6 and 8 above. To convert text values containing both dates and times, use the <a href="#excel-value-function">VALUE function</a>.</li> 
        <li>If the year is omitted in a text date, Excel's DATEVALUE will pick the current year from your computer's system clock, as demonstrated in row 4 above.</li> 
        <li>Since Microsoft Excel stores dates since January 1, 1900 , the use of the Excel DATEVALUE function on earlier dates will result in the #VALUE! error.</li> 
        <li>The DATEVALUE function cannot convert a numeric value to date, nor can it process a text string that looks like a number, for that you will need to use the Excel VALUE function, and this is exactly what we are going to discuss next.</li> 
       </ul> 
       <h3><a name="excel-value-function"></a>Excel VALUE function - convert a text string to date</h3> 
       <p>Compared to DATEVALUE, the Excel VALUE function is more versatile. It can convert any text string that looks like a date or number into a number, which you can easily change to a date format of your choosing.</p> 
       <p>The syntax of the VALUE function is as follows:</p> 
       <p><code>=VALUE(text)</code></p> 
       <p>Where <code>text</code> is a text string or reference to a cell containing the text you want to convert to number.</p> 
       <p>The Excel VALUE function can process both <strong>date and time</strong>, the latter is converted to a decimal portion, as you can see in row 6 in the following screenshot:<br> <img class="imgl2" src="https://cdn.ablebits.com/_img-blog/text-date/excel-value-function.png" alt="Using the Excel VALUE function to convert a text string to date" title="Using the Excel VALUE function to convert a text string to date"></p> 
       <h3><a name="alternativa-formulas"></a>Mathematical operations to convert text to dates</h3> 
       <p>Apart from using specific Excel functions such as VALUE and DATEVALUE, you can perform a simple mathematical operation to force Excel to do a text-to-date conversion for you. The required condition is that an operation <strong>should not</strong> <strong>change the date's value </strong>(serial number). Sounds a bit tricky? The following examples will make things easy!</p> 
       <p>Assuming that your text date is in cell A1, you can use any of the following formulas, and then apply the Date format to the cell:</p> 
       <ul> 
        <li>Addition: <code>=A1 + 0</code></li> 
        <li>Multiplication: <code>=A1 * 1</code></li> 
        <li>Division: <code>=A1 / 1</code></li> 
        <li>Double negation: <code>=--A1</code></li> 
       </ul> 
       <p><img class="imgl2" src="https://cdn.ablebits.com/_img-blog/text-date/convert-text-date-mathematical-operations.png" alt="Converting text to dates via mathematical operations" title="Converting text to dates via mathematical operations"></p> 
       <p>As you can see in the above screenshot, mathematical operations can convert dates (rows 2 and 4), times (row 6) as well as numbers formatted as text (row 8). Sometimes the result is even displayed as a date automatically, and you don't have to bother about changing the cell format.</p> 
       <h3><a name="text2date-custom-delimiters"></a>How to convert text strings with custom delimiters to dates</h3> 
       <p>If your text dates contain some delimiter other than a forward slash (/) or dash (-), Excel functions won't be able to recognize them as dates and return the #VALUE! error.</p> 
       <p>To fix this, you can run Excel's <strong>Find and Replace</strong> tool to replace your delimiter with a slash (/), all in one go:</p> 
       <ul> 
        <li>Select all the text strings you want to convert to dates.</li> 
        <li>Press <span class="hkey-hlight">Ctrl+H</span> to open the <em>Find and Replace</em> dialog box.</li> 
        <li>Enter your custom separator (a dot in this example) in the <em>Find what</em> field, and a slash in the <em>Replace with</em></li> 
        <li>Click the <em>Replace All</em></li> 
       </ul> 
       <p><img class="imgl2" src="https://cdn.ablebits.com/_img-blog/text-date/convert-text-dates-replace-all.png" alt="Replacing a custom delimiter with a slash" title="Replacing a custom delimiter with a slash"></p> 
       <p>Now, the <a href="#excel-datevalue-function">DATEVALUE</a> or <a href="#excel-value-function">VALUE</a> function should have no problem with converting the text strings to dates. In the same manner, you can fix dates containing any other delimiter, e.g. a space or a backward slash.</p> 
       <p>If you prefer a formula solution, you can use Excel's SUBSTITUTE function instead of <em>Replace All</em> to switch your delimiters to slashes.</p> 
       <p>Assuming the text strings are in column A, a SUBSTITUTE formula may look as follows:</p> 
       <p><code>=SUBSTITUTE(A1, ".", "/")</code></p> 
       <p>Where A1 is a text date and "." is the delimiter your strings are separated with.</p> 
       <p>Now, let's embed this SUBSTITUTE function into the VALUE formula:</p> 
       <p><code>=VALUE(SUBSTITUTE(A1, ".", "/"))</code></p> 
       <p>And have the text strings converted to dates, all with a single formula.</p> 
       <p><img class="imgl2" src="https://cdn.ablebits.com/_img-blog/text-date/convert-text-dates-value-substitute.png" alt="Converting text strings with custom delimiters to dates" title="Converting text strings with custom delimiters to dates"></p> 
       <p>As you see, the Excel DATEVALUE and VALUE functions are quite powerful, but both have their limits. For example, if you are trying to convert complex text strings like <em>Thursday, January 01, 2015,</em> neither function could help. Luckily, there is a non-formula solution that can handle this task and the next section explains the detailed steps.</p> 
       <h3><a name="text-to-columns-wizard"></a>Text to Columns wizard - formula-free way to covert text to date</h3> 
       <p>If you are a non-formula user type, a long-standing Excel feature called <em>Text To Columns</em> will come in handy. It can cope with simple text dates demonstrated in <a href="#text2columns-example1">Example 1</a> as well as multi-part text strings shown in <a href="#text2columns-example2">Example 2</a>.</p> 
       <h4><a name="text2columns-example1"></a>Example 1. Converting simple text strings to dates</h4> 
       <p>If the text strings you want to convert to dates look like any of the following:</p> 
       <ul> 
        <li>1.1.2015</li> 
        <li>1.2015</li> 
        <li>01 01 2015</li> 
        <li>2015/1/1</li> 
       </ul> 
       <p>You don't really need formulas, nor exporting or importing anything. All it takes is 5 quick steps.</p> 
       <p>In this example, we will be converting text strings like 01 01 2015 (day, month and year are separated with spaces) to dates.</p> 
       <ol> 
        <li>In your Excel worksheet, select a column of text entries you want to convert to dates.</li> 
        <li>Switch to the <em>Data</em> tab, <em>Data Tools</em> group, and click <strong>Text to Columns.</strong><br> <img class="imgl2" src="https://cdn.ablebits.com/_img-blog/text-date/excel-text-to-columns.png" alt="Switch to the Data tab and click Text to Columns." title="Switch to the Data tab and click Text to Columns."> </li> 
        <li>In step 1 of the <em>Convert Text to Columns Wizard</em>, select <strong>Delimited</strong> and click <em>Next</em>.<br> <img class="imgl2" src="https://cdn.ablebits.com/_img-blog/text-date/excel-convert-text-date.png" alt="In step 1 of the Convert Text to Columns Wizard, select Delimited and click Next." title="In step 1 of the Convert Text to Columns Wizard, select Delimited and click Next."></li> 
        <li>In step 2 of the wizard, uncheck all delimiter boxes and click <em>Next</em>.<br> <img class="imgl2" src="https://cdn.ablebits.com/_img-blog/text-date/excel-convert-text-date2.png" alt="On step 2, uncheck all delimiter boxes and click Next." title="On step 2, uncheck all delimiter boxes and click Next."></li> 
        <li>In the final step, select <strong>Date</strong> under <em>Column data format,</em> choose the format<strong> corresponding to your dates</strong>, and click <em>Finish.</em></li> 
       </ol> 
       <p>In this example, we are converting the text dates formatted as "01 02 2015" (month day year), so we select <em>MDY</em> from the drop down box.<br> <img class="imgl2" src="https://cdn.ablebits.com/_img-blog/text-date/excel-convert-text-date3.png" alt="Choose the format corresponding to your dates, and click Finish." title="Choose the format corresponding to your dates, and click Finish."></p> 
       <p>Now, Excel recognizes your text strings as dates, automatically converts them to your default date format and displays right-aligned in the cells. You can <a href="https://www.ablebits.com/office-addins-blog/2015/03/11/change-date-format-excel/#change-date-format">change the date format</a> in the usual way via the <em>Format Cells</em> dialog.</p> 
       <div class="sm-note">
        <b>Note.</b> For the 
        <em>Text to Column</em> wizard to work correctly, all of your text strings should be formatted identically. For example, if some of your entries are formatted like 
        <em>day/month/year</em> format while others are 
        <em>month/day/year</em>, you would get incorrect results.
       </div> 
       <h4><a name="text2columns-example2"></a>Example 2. Converting complex text strings to dates</h4> 
       <p>If your dates are represented by multi-part text strings, such as:</p> 
       <ul> 
        <li>Thursday, January 01, 2015</li> 
        <li>January 01, 2015 3 PM</li> 
       </ul> 
       <p>You will have to put a bit more effort and use both the <em>Text to Columns</em> wizard and Excel DATE function.</p> 
       <ol> 
        <li>Select all text strings to be converted to dates.</li> 
        <li>Click the <strong>Text to Columns</strong> button on the <em>Data</em> tab, <em>Data Tools</em> group.</li> 
        <li>On step 1 of the <em>Convert Text to Columns Wizard</em>, select <strong>Delimited</strong> and click <em>Next</em>.</li> 
        <li>On step 2 of the wizard, select the delimiters your text strings contain. <p> For example, if you are converting strings separated by commas and spaces, like "<em>Thursday, January 01, 2015"</em>, you should choose both delimiters - Comma and Space.<br> <img class="imgl2" src="https://cdn.ablebits.com/_img-blog/text-date/convert-text-strings-dates.png" alt="Select the delimiters your text strings contain." title="Select the delimiters your text strings contain."></p> <p> It also makes sense to select the "<em>Treat consecutive delimiters as one</em>" option to ignore extra spaces, if your data has any.</p> <p> And finally, have a look at the <em>Data preview</em> window and verify if the text strings are split to columns correctly, then click <em>Next</em>. </p></li> 
        <li>On step 3 of the wizard, make sure all columns in the Data Preview section have the <strong>General</strong> format. If they don't, click on a column and select <em>General</em> under the <em>Column data format</em> options. 
         <div class="sm-note">
          <b>Note.</b> Do not choose the 
          <em>Date</em> format for any column because each column contains only one component, so Excel won't be able to understand this is a date.
         </div> <p> If you don't need some column, click on it and select <em>Do not import column (skip).</em></p> <p> If you don't want to overwrite the original data, specify where the columns should be inserted - enter the address for the top left cell in the <em>Destination</em> field.</p> <p> When done, click the <em>Finish</em> button.<br> <img class="imgl2" src="https://cdn.ablebits.com/_img-blog/text-date/convert-text-strings-dates2.png" alt="Make sure all columns have the General format and choose where to insert the columns." title="Make sure all columns have the General format and choose where to insert the columns."></p> <p> As you see in the screenshot above, we are skipping the first column with the days of the week, splitting the other data into 3 columns (in the <em>General</em> format) and inserting these columns beginning from cell C2.</p> <p> The following screenshot shows the result, with the original data in column A and the split data in columns C, D and E.</p> <p> <img class="imgl2" src="https://cdn.ablebits.com/_img-blog/text-date/excel-text-columns-result.png" alt="Text strings are split into 3 different columns." title="Text strings are split into 3 different columns."></p> </li>
        <li>Finally, you have to combine the date parts together by using a DATE formula. The syntax of the Excel DATE function is self-explanatory: <p> <code>=DATE(year, month, day)</code></p> <p> In our case, <code>year</code> is in column E and <code>day</code> is in column D, no problem with these.</p> <p> It's not so easy with <code>month</code> because it is text while the DATE function needs a number. Luckily, Microsoft Excel provides a special MONTH function that can change a month's name to a month's number:</p> <p> <code>=MONTH(serial_number)</code></p> <p> For the MONTH function to understand it deals with a date, we put it like this:</p> <p> <code>=MONTH(1&amp;C2)</code></p> <p> Where C2 contains the name of the month, <em>January</em> in our case. "1&amp;" is added to concatenate a date (<em>1 January)</em> so that the MONTH function can convert it to the corresponding month number.</p> <p> And now, let's embed the MONTH function into the <code>month</code>; argument of our DATE formula:</p> <p> <code>=DATE(F2,MONTH(1&amp;D2),E2)</code></p></li> 
       </ol> 
       <p>And voila, our complex text strings are successfully converted to dates:<br> <img class="imgl2" src="https://cdn.ablebits.com/_img-blog/text-date/convert-text-strings-dates-result.png" alt="The text strings are successfully converted to dates." title="The text strings are successfully converted to dates."></p> 
       <h3><a name="text2date-paste-special"></a>Quick conversion of text dates using Paste Special</h3> 
       <p>To quickly convert a range of simple text strings to dates, you can use the following trick.</p> 
       <ul> 
        <li>Copy any empty cell (select it and press <span class="hkey-hlight">Ctrl+C</span>).</li> 
        <li>Select the range with text values you want to convert to dates.</li> 
        <li>Right-click the selection, click <strong>Paste Special</strong>, and select <strong>Add</strong> in the <em>Paste Special</em> dialog box:<br> <img class="imgl2" src="https://cdn.ablebits.com/_img-blog/text-date/convert-text-dates-paste-special.png" alt="Quick conversion of text dates using Paste Special" title="Quick conversion of text dates using Paste Special"></li> 
        <li>Click <em>OK</em> to complete the conversion and close the dialog.</li> 
       </ul> 
       <p>What you have just done is tell Excel to add a zero (empty cell) to your text dates. To be able to do this, Excel converts a text string to a number, and since adding a zero does not change the value, you get exactly what you wanted - the date's serial number. As usual, you <a href="#excel-datevalue-function">change a number to the date format</a> by using the <em>Format Cells</em> dialog.</p> 
       <p>To learn more about the Paste Special feature, please see <a href="https://www.ablebits.com/office-addins-blog/2016/10/20/excel-paste-special-shortcuts-features/">How to use Paste Special in Excel</a></p> 
       <h3><a name="text2date-two-digit-years"></a>Fixing text dates with two-digit years</h3> 
       <p>The modern versions of Microsoft Excel are smart enough to spot some obvious errors in your data, or better say, what Excel considers an error. When this happens, you will see an error indicator (a small green triangle) in the upper-left corner of the cell and when you select the cell, an exclamation mark appears:<br> <img class="imgl2" src="https://cdn.ablebits.com/_img-blog/text-date/text-number-error-indicator.png" alt="Error indicators in Excel" title="Error indicators in Excel"></p> 
       <p>Clicking the exclamation mark will display a few options relevant to your data. In case of a 2-digit year, Excel will ask if you want to convert it to 19XX or 20XX.</p> 
       <p>If you have multiple entries of this type, you can fix them all in one fell swoop - select all the cells with errors, then click on the exclamation mark and select the appropriate option.<br> <img class="imgl2" src="https://cdn.ablebits.com/_img-blog/text-date/convert-two-digits-years.png" alt="Fixing text dates with two-digit years using Excel Error Checking" title="Fixing text dates with two-digit years using Excel Error Checking"></p> 
       <h4>How to turn on Error Checking in Excel</h4> 
       <p>Usually, Error Checking is enabled in Excel by default. To make sure, click <em>File</em> &gt; <em>Options</em> &gt; <em>Formulas</em>, scroll down to the<em> Error Checking</em> section and verify if the following options are checked:</p> 
       <ul> 
        <li><em>Enable background error checking</em> under <em>Error Checking</em>;</li> 
        <li><em>Cells containing years represented as 2 digits</em> under <em>Error checking rules</em>.</li> 
       </ul> 
       <p><img class="imgl2" src="https://cdn.ablebits.com/_img-blog/text-date/enable-error-checking.png" alt="Turning on Error Checking in Excel" title="Turning on Error Checking in Excel"></p> 
       <p>This is how you convert text to date in Excel and change dates to text. Hopefully, you have been able to find a technique to your liking. In the next article, we will tackle the opposite task and explore different ways of converting Excel dates to text strings. I thank you for reading and hope to see you next week.</p> 
       <h3>You may also be interested in:</h3>

        <li><a href="https://www.ablebits.com/office-addins-blog/2014/06/17/excel-conditional-formatting-dates/">How to conditionally format dates in Excel</a></li>

             <p>John,</p> 
             <p>This article explains how to convert text to date in Excel.</p> 
             <p>To prevent Excel from converting your data to a date, type an apostrophe (') before it, e.g. '1/1/2015. In this case, the input data will be a text string.</p> 
             <p>To convert existing dates to text strings, you can use the TEXT function or Text to Columns wizard, as demonstrated in <a href="https://www.ablebits.com/office-addins-blog/2015/04/08/convert-date-text-excel/" rel="nofollow">How to convert date to text in Excel</a>.</p>

           <div id="comment-162392"> 
            <div class="comment-author vcard"> 
             <img alt="" src="https://secure.gravatar.com/avatar/d18b5882ffacf3784d76e45472449587?s=40&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g" srcset="https://secure.gravatar.com/avatar/d18b5882ffacf3784d76e45472449587?s=80&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x" class="avatar avatar-40 photo" height="40" width="40"> 
             <cite class="fn"><a href="http://www.ablebits.com" rel="external nofollow" class="url">Svetlana Cheusheva</a></cite> 
             <span class="says">says:</span> 
            </div>
            <!-- .comment-author .vcard --> 
            <div class="comment-meta commentmetadata">
             <a href="https://www.ablebits.com/office-addins-blog/2015/03/26/excel-convert-text-date/#comment-162392"> July 15, 2015 at 9:37 am</a> 
            </div>
            <!-- .comment-meta .commentmetadata --> 
            <div class="comment-body">
             <p>Hi Ryan,</p> 
             <p>When you are concatenating a text string and a formula-driven date, you have to use the TEXT function to display the date in the desired format. For example:<br> =CONCATENATE("Today is ", TEXT(TODAY(), "mm/dd/yy"))<br> or<br> ="Today is " &amp; TEXT(TODAY(), "mm/dd/yy")</p> 
            </div> 
            <div class="reply"> 
             <a rel="nofollow" class="comment-reply-link" href="https://www.ablebits.com/office-addins-blog/2015/03/26/excel-convert-text-date/?replytocom=162392#respond" onclick="return addComment.moveForm( &quot;comment-162392&quot;, &quot;162392&quot;, &quot;respond&quot;, &quot;8481&quot; )" aria-label="Reply to Svetlana Cheusheva">Reply</a>

            <!-- .comment-author .vcard --> 
            <div class="comment-meta commentmetadata">
             <a href="https://www.ablebits.com/office-addins-blog/2015/03/26/excel-convert-text-date/#comment-166654"> August 12, 2015 at 9:37 am</a> 
            </div>
            <!-- .comment-meta .commentmetadata --> 
            <div class="comment-body">
             <p>Hi!</p> 
             <p>You can use the following formula where A1 is a cell with the date:<br> =DATE(MID(A1,7,2), MID(A1,4,2), MID(A1,1,2)) + TIME(MID(A1,10,2), MID(A1,13,2),0)</p> 
            </div> 
            <div class="reply"> 
             <a rel="nofollow" class="comment-reply-link" href="https://www.ablebits.com/office-addins-blog/2015/03/26/excel-convert-text-date/?replytocom=166654#respond" onclick="return addComment.moveForm( &quot;comment-166654&quot;, &quot;166654&quot;, &quot;respond&quot;, &quot;8481&quot; )" aria-label="Reply to Svetlana Cheusheva">Reply</a>

            <li class="comment byuser comment-author-svetlana-cheusheva bypostauthor odd alt depth-3" id="li-comment-191067"> 
             <div id="comment-191067"> 
              <div class="comment-author vcard"> 
               <img alt="" src="https://secure.gravatar.com/avatar/d18b5882ffacf3784d76e45472449587?s=40&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g" srcset="https://secure.gravatar.com/avatar/d18b5882ffacf3784d76e45472449587?s=80&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x" class="avatar avatar-40 photo" height="40" width="40"> 
               <cite class="fn"><a href="http://www.ablebits.com" rel="external nofollow" class="url">Svetlana Cheusheva</a></cite> 
               <span class="says">says:</span> 
              </div>
              <!-- .comment-author .vcard --> 
              <div class="comment-meta commentmetadata">
               <a href="https://www.ablebits.com/office-addins-blog/2015/03/26/excel-convert-text-date/#comment-191067"> February 1, 2016 at 3:13 pm</a> 
              </div>
              <!-- .comment-meta .commentmetadata --> 
              <div class="comment-body">
               <p>Hi Reed,</p> 
               <p>It's next to impossible to write a formula for this particular example, because the first item (supposedly a month number) contains just one digit (8). In other dates, there can be 2 digits, and no algorithm is smart enough to distinguish between these cases. </p> 
               <p>If your source data had a leading zero, i.e. 081215182533 (mmddyyhhmmss format), then you could use the following formula:</p> 
               <p>=DATE(MID(A1,5,2), LEFT(A1,2), MID(A1,2,2)) + TIME(MID(A1,7,2), MID(A1,9,2),RIGHT(A1, 2))</p> 
              </div> 
              <div class="reply"> 
               <a rel="nofollow" class="comment-reply-link" href="https://www.ablebits.com/office-addins-blog/2015/03/26/excel-convert-text-date/?replytocom=191067#respond" onclick="return addComment.moveForm( &quot;comment-191067&quot;, &quot;191067&quot;, &quot;respond&quot;, &quot;8481&quot; )" aria-label="Reply to Svetlana Cheusheva">Reply</a> 
              </div>

            <!-- .comment-author .vcard --> 
            <div class="comment-meta commentmetadata">
             <a href="https://www.ablebits.com/office-addins-blog/2015/03/26/excel-convert-text-date/#comment-215863"> November 2, 2016 at 9:06 pm</a> 
            </div>
            <!-- .comment-meta .commentmetadata --> 
            <div class="comment-body">
             <p>Reed, this is probably way too late to help, but I solved a similar issue today. My date column was written as plain text and did not have leading zeroes. </p> 
             <p>The date, March 19, 2015 was written as 31915.</p> 
             <p>DateText in cell A2<br> 31915 </p> 
             <p>Based on this page and some other searches, I used this formula:<br> =DATE( YEAR , MONTH , DAY )<br> =DATE((20&amp;RIGHT(A2,2)),LEFT(A2, LEN(A2)-4),LEFT(RIGHT(A2,4),2))</p> 
             <p>HTH someone,<br> Wayne</p> 
            </div>

              <!-- .comment-meta .commentmetadata --> 
              <div class="comment-body">
               <p>Hello SAGAR,</p> 
               <p>The DATEVALUE function converts a date in the text format to a serial number that Microsoft Excel recognizes as a date. </p> 
               <p>For example: =DATEVALUE("1/1/2015")</p> 
               <p>You can find a few more examples on the following page:<br> <a href="https://www.ablebits.com/office-addins-blog/2015/06/10/excel-date-functions/#DATEVALUE" rel="nofollow">https://www.ablebits.com/office-addins-blog/2015/06/10/excel-date-functions/#DATEVALUE</a></p> 
              </div> 
              <div class="reply"> 
               <a rel="nofollow" class="comment-reply-link" href="https://www.ablebits.com/office-addins-blog/2015/03/26/excel-convert-text-date/?replytocom=168419#respond" onclick="return addComment.moveForm( &quot;comment-168419&quot;, &quot;168419&quot;, &quot;respond&quot;, &quot;8481&quot; )" aria-label="Reply to Svetlana Cheusheva">Reply</a>

             <p>Hi Tony,</p> 
             <p>Select the cell(s), press Ctrl+1 to open the Format Cells dialog, switch to Custom and type the format code mmm-dd in the Type box.</p> 
             <p>The following page provides the detailed step-by-step instructions along with the codes:<br> <a href="https://www.ablebits.com/office-addins-blog/2015/03/11/change-date-format-excel/#custom-date-format" rel="nofollow">https://www.ablebits.com/office-addins-blog/2015/03/11/change-date-format-excel/#custom-date-format</a></p>

            <!-- .comment-author .vcard --> 
            <div class="comment-meta commentmetadata">
             <a href="https://www.ablebits.com/office-addins-blog/2015/03/26/excel-convert-text-date/#comment-189499"> January 19, 2016 at 9:50 am</a> 
            </div>
            <!-- .comment-meta .commentmetadata --> 
            <div class="comment-body">
             <p>Hi Deepak,</p> 
             <p>First, divide 6 by 24 (there are 24 hrs in a day). The formula can be as simple as =A1/24. This will yield the decimal value (for 6 the result will be 0.25). </p> 
             <p>Now, select the cell with the formula result, right-click and select Format Cells from the context menu. The Format Cells dialog will appear, you choose Time on the left pane, and the format you want on the right pane under Type. Please see the following example for full details: <a href="https://www.ablebits.com/office-addins-blog/2015/07/01/excel-convert-time-decimal/#convert-number-time" rel="nofollow">How to convert numbers to time format in Excel</a>.</p> 
            </div> 
            <div class="reply"> 
             <a rel="nofollow" class="comment-reply-link" href="https://www.ablebits.com/office-addins-blog/2015/03/26/excel-convert-text-date/?replytocom=189499#respond" onclick="return addComment.moveForm( &quot;comment-189499&quot;, &quot;189499&quot;, &quot;respond&quot;, &quot;8481&quot; )" aria-label="Reply to Svetlana Cheusheva">Reply</a>

              <li class="comment byuser comment-author-svetlana-cheusheva bypostauthor even depth-4" id="li-comment-190468"> 
               <div id="comment-190468"> 
                <div class="comment-author vcard"> 
                 <img alt="" src="https://secure.gravatar.com/avatar/d18b5882ffacf3784d76e45472449587?s=40&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g" srcset="https://secure.gravatar.com/avatar/d18b5882ffacf3784d76e45472449587?s=80&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x" class="avatar avatar-40 photo" height="40" width="40"> 
                 <cite class="fn"><a href="http://www.ablebits.com" rel="external nofollow" class="url">Svetlana Cheusheva</a></cite> 
                 <span class="says">says:</span> 
                </div>
                <!-- .comment-author .vcard --> 
                <div class="comment-meta commentmetadata">
                 <a href="https://www.ablebits.com/office-addins-blog/2015/03/26/excel-convert-text-date/#comment-190468"> January 27, 2016 at 1:25 pm</a> 
                </div>
                <!-- .comment-meta .commentmetadata --> 
                <div class="comment-body">
                 <p>Hi Hafiz,</p> 
                 <p>From your example, it's not quite clear which of the two 01 is month and which is day. </p> 
                 <p>Assuming your source dates (20160101) are in the format "yyyymmdd", you can use the following formula:<br> =DATE(LEFT(A1,4),MID(A1,5,2),RIGHT(A1,2))</p> 
                 <p>If it is the "yyyyddmm" format, then change the order of the last 2 arguments:<br> =DATE(LEFT(A1,4),RIGHT(A1,2),MID(A1,5,2))</p> 
                 <p>Both formulas return serial numbers representing the dates in the internal Excel system. To have the output formatted as date, select a cell with the formula, right click, click "Format Cells", and choose the date format you want.</p> 
                </div> 
                <div class="reply"> 
                 <a rel="nofollow" class="comment-reply-link" href="https://www.ablebits.com/office-addins-blog/2015/03/26/excel-convert-text-date/?replytocom=190468#respond" onclick="return addComment.moveForm( &quot;comment-190468&quot;, &quot;190468&quot;, &quot;respond&quot;, &quot;8481&quot; )" aria-label="Reply to Svetlana Cheusheva">Reply</a>

            <!-- .comment-author .vcard --> 
            <div class="comment-meta commentmetadata">
             <a href="https://www.ablebits.com/office-addins-blog/2015/03/26/excel-convert-text-date/#comment-190467"> January 27, 2016 at 1:17 pm</a> 
            </div>
            <!-- .comment-meta .commentmetadata --> 
            <div class="comment-body">
             <p>Hi Raman,</p> 
             <p>You can use the following formula (where A2 is the source date):</p> 
             <p>=DATE(YEAR(A2), MONTH(A2) + 18, DAY(A2))</p> 
            </div> 
            <div class="reply"> 
             <a rel="nofollow" class="comment-reply-link" href="https://www.ablebits.com/office-addins-blog/2015/03/26/excel-convert-text-date/?replytocom=190467#respond" onclick="return addComment.moveForm( &quot;comment-190467&quot;, &quot;190467&quot;, &quot;respond&quot;, &quot;8481&quot; )" aria-label="Reply to Svetlana Cheusheva">Reply</a>

             <img alt="" src="https://secure.gravatar.com/avatar/d18b5882ffacf3784d76e45472449587?s=40&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g" srcset="https://secure.gravatar.com/avatar/d18b5882ffacf3784d76e45472449587?s=80&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x" class="avatar avatar-40 photo" height="40" width="40"> 
             <cite class="fn"><a href="http://www.ablebits.com" rel="external nofollow" class="url">Svetlana Cheusheva</a></cite> 
             <span class="says">says:</span> 
            </div>
            <!-- .comment-author .vcard --> 
            <div class="comment-meta commentmetadata">
             <a href="https://www.ablebits.com/office-addins-blog/2015/03/26/excel-convert-text-date/#comment-191485"> February 5, 2016 at 1:56 pm</a> 
            </div>
            <!-- .comment-meta .commentmetadata --> 
            <div class="comment-body">
             <p>Hi Jose,</p> 
             <p>You can use the following formula to convert your dates to text in the specified format:<br> =TEXT(A1, "mmm yy")</p> 
             <p>Or, to change only the display format, select the cells, right-click, then click Format Cells... and set custom format to mmm yy.</p> 
             <p>The difference is that the formula converts a date to a text value, while setting a custom format to a cell keeps the original value and changes only the visual representation of a date.</p> 
            </div> 
            <div class="reply"> 
             <a rel="nofollow" class="comment-reply-link" href="https://www.ablebits.com/office-addins-blog/2015/03/26/excel-convert-text-date/?replytocom=191485#respond" onclick="return addComment.moveForm( &quot;comment-191485&quot;, &quot;191485&quot;, &quot;respond&quot;, &quot;8481&quot; )" aria-label="Reply to Svetlana Cheusheva">Reply</a>

            </div>
            <!-- .comment-author .vcard --> 
            <div class="comment-meta commentmetadata">
             <a href="https://www.ablebits.com/office-addins-blog/2015/03/26/excel-convert-text-date/#comment-191484"> February 5, 2016 at 1:50 pm</a> 
            </div>
            <!-- .comment-meta .commentmetadata --> 
            <div class="comment-body">
             <p>Hello Sachin,</p> 
             <p>To keep the source data and change only the display format, you can select the cells, press Ctrl+1 to open the Format Cells dialog, select custom under Category on the left pane, and type mmm-yyyy in the Type box.</p> 
             <p>To convert the dates to text, use the following formula:<br> =TEXT(A1, "mmm-yyyy")</p> 
             <p>Where A1 is the source date you want to convert.</p> 
            </div>

            <div class="comment-body">
             <p>Hi PM,</p> 
             <p>You simply need to replace formulas with their calculated values. To do this, select the entire date column, press Ctrl+C to copy it, then right-click the selection and click Paste Special &gt; Values. Done!</p> 
            </div>

            <div class="comment-meta commentmetadata">

            </div>
            <!-- .comment-meta .commentmetadata --> 
            <div class="comment-body">
             <p>Hi Avnish,</p> 
             <p>You can use the following formulas, where A1 is a cell with a date:</p> 
             <p>To extract a year: =LEFT(A1, 4)</p> 
             <p>To extract a month: =TEXT(DATE(LEFT(A1, 4), RIGHT(A1, 2), 1), "mmmm")</p> 
            </div> 
            <div class="reply"> 
             <a rel="nofollow" class="comment-reply-link" href="https://www.ablebits.com/office-addins-blog/2015/03/26/excel-convert-text-date/?replytocom=193260#respond" onclick="return addComment.moveForm( &quot;comment-193260&quot;, &quot;193260&quot;, &quot;respond&quot;, &quot;8481&quot; )" aria-label="Reply to Svetlana Cheusheva">Reply</a> 
            </div>
            <!-- .reply --> 
           </div>
           <!-- #comment-##  --> </li>

            <div class="comment-meta commentmetadata">
             <a href="https://www.ablebits.com/office-addins-blog/2015/03/26/excel-convert-text-date/#comment-193383"> March 4, 2016 at 9:36 am</a> 
            </div>
            <!-- .comment-meta .commentmetadata --> 
            <div class="comment-body">
             <p>Hi Ahmed,</p> 
             <p>You can do it using the following formula:</p> 
             <p>=DATE(RIGHT(A1,4), MID(A1,3,2), LEFT(A1,2))</p> 
             <p>Where A1 is a cell containing the original date.</p> 
            </div>

           <div id="comment-194691"> 
            <div class="comment-author vcard"> 
             <img alt="" src="https://secure.gravatar.com/avatar/d18b5882ffacf3784d76e45472449587?s=40&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g" srcset="https://secure.gravatar.com/avatar/d18b5882ffacf3784d76e45472449587?s=80&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x" class="avatar avatar-40 photo" height="40" width="40"> 
             <cite class="fn"><a href="http://www.ablebits.com" rel="external nofollow" class="url">Svetlana Cheusheva</a></cite> 
             <span class="says">says:</span> 
            </div>
            <!-- .comment-author .vcard --> 
            <div class="comment-meta commentmetadata">
             <a href="https://www.ablebits.com/office-addins-blog/2015/03/26/excel-convert-text-date/#comment-194691"> March 23, 2016 at 9:53 am</a> 
            </div>
            <!-- .comment-meta .commentmetadata --> 
            <div class="comment-body">
             <p>Hi William,</p> 
             <p>Try the following formula, where A1 is the cell with a date.</p> 
             <p>=TEXT(A1, "yyyymmdd")</p> 
             <p>Please keep in mind that the result of the TEXT function is always a text string, and therefore if you want to output a number, wrap it in the NUMBERVALUE function:</p> 
             <p>=NUMBERVALUE(TEXT(A1, "yyyymmdd"))</p> 
            </div> 
            <div class="reply"> 
             <a rel="nofollow" class="comment-reply-link" href="https://www.ablebits.com/office-addins-blog/2015/03/26/excel-convert-text-date/?replytocom=194691#respond" onclick="return addComment.moveForm( &quot;comment-194691&quot;, &quot;194691&quot;, &quot;respond&quot;, &quot;8481&quot; )" aria-label="Reply to Svetlana Cheusheva">Reply</a>

        <li class="comment even thread-even depth-1" id="li-comment-194985">

          <li class="comment byuser comment-author-svetlana-cheusheva bypostauthor odd alt depth-2" id="li-comment-201348"> 
           <div id="comment-201348"> 
            <div class="comment-author vcard"> 
             <img alt="" src="https://secure.gravatar.com/avatar/d18b5882ffacf3784d76e45472449587?s=40&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g" srcset="https://secure.gravatar.com/avatar/d18b5882ffacf3784d76e45472449587?s=80&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x" class="avatar avatar-40 photo" height="40" width="40"> 
             <cite class="fn"><a href="http://www.ablebits.com" rel="external nofollow" class="url">Svetlana Cheusheva</a></cite> 
             <span class="says">says:</span> 
            </div>
            <!-- .comment-author .vcard --> 
            <div class="comment-meta commentmetadata">
             <a href="https://www.ablebits.com/office-addins-blog/2015/03/26/excel-convert-text-date/#comment-201348"> May 23, 2016 at 11:18 am</a> 
            </div>
            <!-- .comment-meta .commentmetadata --> 
            <div class="comment-body">
             <p>Hello!</p> 
             <p>You can use the following formula to return the first day of the month of the date in A1:<br> =DATE(YEAR(A1), MONTH(A1), 1)</p> 
             <p>After that, press Ctrl+1 to open the Format Cells dialog, on the left-side pane under 'Category' choose Custom, and type the following format in the Type box: mm/dd/yyyy</p> 
            </div> 
            <div class="reply"> 
             <a rel="nofollow" class="comment-reply-link" href="https://www.ablebits.com/office-addins-blog/2015/03/26/excel-convert-text-date/?replytocom=201348#respond" onclick="return addComment.moveForm( &quot;comment-201348&quot;, &quot;201348&quot;, &quot;respond&quot;, &quot;8481&quot; )" aria-label="Reply to Svetlana Cheusheva">Reply</a>

            <!-- .comment-meta .commentmetadata --> 
            <div class="comment-body">
             <p>Hi Tim,</p> 
             <p>If your dates are entered as dates and not as text strings, select all the dates you want to re-format, press Ctrl+1 to open the Format Cell dialog, select Custom under Category, and type the following format in the Type box: mm/d/yyyy</p> 
            </div>

             <a rel="nofollow" class="comment-reply-link" href="https://www.ablebits.com/office-addins-blog/2015/03/26/excel-convert-text-date/?replytocom=206862#respond" onclick="return addComment.moveForm( &quot;comment-206862&quot;, &quot;206862&quot;, &quot;respond&quot;, &quot;8481&quot; )" aria-label="Reply to Svetlana Cheusheva">Reply</a>

            <!-- .comment-meta .commentmetadata --> 
            <div class="comment-body">
             <p>Dear Socheata,</p> 
             <p>You can easily do this by changing the cell format:</p> 
             <p>Select the cell(s) with dates, press Ctrl+1 to open the Format Cells dialog, select Custom under Category, and type the format code dd-mmm-yy in the Type box. That's it!</p> 
             <p>For the detailed instructions, please see <a href="https://www.ablebits.com/office-addins-blog/2015/03/11/change-date-format-excel/#custom-date-format">How to change the date format in Excel</a>.</p>

             <p>Hi, Izzy,</p> 
             <p>activate the cell with a text you want to transform, then under the <strong>Home</strong> tab find <em>Number</em> format box, and choose <em>Long Date</em> or <em>Short Date</em> to your liking. If it already says <em>Date</em> – your data is ready for calculations.</p>

             <div id="comment-292973"> 
              <div class="comment-author vcard"> 
               <img alt="" src="https://secure.gravatar.com/avatar/?s=40&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g" srcset="https://secure.gravatar.com/avatar/?s=80&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x" class="avatar avatar-40 photo avatar-default" height="40" width="40"> 
               <cite class="fn">Dusty</cite> 
               <span class="says">says:</span> 
              </div>
              <!-- .comment-author .vcard --> 
              <div class="comment-meta commentmetadata">
               <a href="https://www.ablebits.com/office-addins-blog/2015/03/26/excel-convert-text-date/#comment-292973"> July 19, 2017 at 5:26 pm</a> 
              </div>
              <!-- .comment-meta .commentmetadata --> 
              <div class="comment-body">
               <p>one way around is<br> =DATE(RIGHT(E3,4), LEFT(E3,len(e3)-6), MID(E3,3,len(e3-5)))</p> 
               <p>this way it can change the spot it starts reading the number from depending on the length of the number string since it doesn't see the lead 0</p> 
              </div> 
              <div class="reply"> 
               <a rel="nofollow" class="comment-reply-link" href="https://www.ablebits.com/office-addins-blog/2015/03/26/excel-convert-text-date/?replytocom=292973#respond" onclick="return addComment.moveForm( &quot;comment-292973&quot;, &quot;292973&quot;, &quot;respond&quot;, &quot;8481&quot; )" aria-label="Reply to Dusty">Reply</a>
